### Post by markbuntu on 2009-05-20
> **sh1ma_tetsu0 said:**
> No luck for me, installation of Catalyst 9.5 on Ubuntu 9.04 fails, as it was with Catalyst 9.4, dkms is saying something about "missing patch", and after restart X server fails to start. :-k

That is most likely the rt kernel patch that dkms cannot find since you are using ubuntustudio and the rt kernel. 

This patch was misplaced in 9.4 and I told them that but it looks like they did not fix it with 9.5. I filed a bug report on the missing patch back in Feb on 9.1 and they said they fixed it for 9.4 (fglrx8.600).....and there has been no reply recently from Mario Limoncello who is the Ubuntu maintainer. Maybe he is on extended holiday, lol.

[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/fglrx-installer/+bug/328856](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/fglrx-installer/+bug/328856)

You should file a new bug report to get someone's attention.

You should remove the driver with the fglrx-uninstall.sh script in usr/share/ati if you want to use the rt kernel with the open source drivers. This is important since fglrx replaces some xorg libs that the open source drivers need and the script should return them.

---

### Post by LinuxTAd on 2009-05-20
New install everything runs great here is my current config, even got the dual monitors to work the way I want them too!  Xinerama!!!


```


# xorg.conf (X.Org X Window System server configuration file)
#
# This file was generated by dexconf, the Debian X Configuration tool, using
# values from the debconf database.
#
# Edit this file with caution, and see the xorg.conf manual page.
# (Type "man xorg.conf" at the shell prompt.)
#
# This file is automatically updated on xserver-xorg package upgrades *only*
# if it has not been modified since the last upgrade of the xserver-xorg
# package.
#
# Note that some configuration settings that could be done previously
# in this file, now are automatically configured by the server and settings
# here are ignored.
#
# If you have edited this file but would like it to be automatically updated
# again, run the following command:
#   sudo dpkg-reconfigure -phigh xserver-xorg

Section "ServerLayout"
    Identifier     "aticonfig Layout"
    Screen      0  "aticonfig-Screen[0]-0" 0 0
    Screen         "amdcccle-Screen[1]-1" RightOf "aticonfig-Screen[0]-0"
EndSection

Section "Files"
EndSection

Section "Module"
EndSection

Section "ServerFlags"
    Option        "Xinerama" "on"
EndSection

Section "Monitor"
    Identifier   "aticonfig-Monitor[0]-0"
    Option        "VendorName" "ATI Proprietary Driver"
    Option        "ModelName" "Generic Autodetecting Monitor"
    Option        "DPMS" "true"
EndSection

Section "Monitor"
    Identifier   "amdcccle-Monitor[1]-1"
    Option        "VendorName" "ATI Proprietary Driver"
    Option        "ModelName" "Generic Autodetecting Monitor"
    Option        "DPMS" "true"
EndSection

Section "Device"
    Identifier  "aticonfig-Device[0]-0"
    Driver      "fglrx"
    Option        "UseFastTLS" "1"
    Option        "VideoOverlay" "on"
    Option        "OpenGLOverlay" "off"
    Option        "EnableRandR12" "false"
#    Option        "DesktopSetup" "horizontal"
    BusID       "PCI:1:0:0"
EndSection

Section "Device"
    Identifier  "amdcccle-Device[1]-1"
    Driver      "fglrx"
    BusID       "PCI:1:0:0"
    Screen      1
EndSection

Section "Screen"
    Identifier "aticonfig-Screen[0]-0"
    Device     "aticonfig-Device[0]-0"
    Monitor    "aticonfig-Monitor[0]-0"
    DefaultDepth     24
    SubSection "Display"
        Viewport   0 0
        Depth     24
    EndSubSection
EndSection

Section "Screen"
    Identifier "amdcccle-Screen[1]-1"
    Device     "amdcccle-Device[1]-1"
    Monitor    "amdcccle-Monitor[1]-1"
    DefaultDepth     24
    SubSection "Display"
        Viewport   0 0
        Depth     24
    EndSubSection
EndSection


####################  Logitech G5  Mouse  Buttons  ###################


Section "InputDevice"
    Identifier "Configured Mouse"
    Driver "mouse"
    Option "CorePointer"
    Option "Device" "/dev/input/mice"
    Option "Protocol" "auto"
    Option "Buttons" "7" # Tells X11 the number of buttons on the mouse
    Option "ZAxisMapping" "4 5" # Tells X11 which buttons to use for scrolling, 4 is up, 5 is down
    Option "ButtonMapping" "1 2 3 6 7 4 5"
EndSection

```

### Post by Melcar on 2009-05-21
Uninstall fglrx, generate a new xorg.conf, and edit it to load the desired drivers.
How to uninstall fglrx will depend on how you installed it in the first place.  If you used packages, then simply remove them with Synaptic.  If you used the .run file from ATI's website, simply run:

```
cd /usr/share/ati
sudo sh ./fglrx-uninstall.sh
```

After this, generate a new xorg.conf file:

```
sudo dpkg-reconfigure xsrever-xorg
```

Finally, open up xorg.conf and make the necessary changes:

```
sudo gedit /etc/X11/xorg.conf

#look for the *Device* section and append the option:
#Driver    "radeon"
```

Save the file and reboot.

---

How to uninstall fglrx will depend on how you installed it in the first place.  If you used packages, then simply remove them with Synaptic.  If you used the .run file from ATI's website, simply run:

```
cd /usr/share/ati
sudo sh ./fglrx-uninstall.sh
```

After this, generate a new xorg.conf file:

```
sudo dpkg-reconfigure xsrever-xorg
```

Finally, open up xorg.conf and make the necessary changes:

```
sudo gedit /etc/X11/xorg.conf

#look for the *Device* section and append the option:
#Driver    "radeon"
```

Save the file and reboot.

### Post by tommo12 on 2009-05-25
My problem is, When i tried to upgrade last time,  I ran the script, - sh ./fglrx-uninstall.sh, then rebooted, ready to install the new GUI based driver that I had downloaded (atd i-driver-installer-9-5-x86.x86_64.run) But when it started up it froze because I had taken the driver away, I mean I could get into the safemode terminal screen. But not into the GUI wheere I would install the new driver.... so I don't make this mistake again wat do you ppl suggest I do and please break it down for this noob.

[COLOR=Orange](ATI MANUAL)
I have read teh ATI install manual

1 Launch the Terminal Application/Window and navigate to the /usr/share/ati folder.
  With superuser permissions, enter the command "sh ./fglrx-uninstall.sh".
2
  Reboot your system.
3[/COLOR]

### Post by zika on 2009-05-25
> **tommo12 said:**
> My problem is, When i tried to upgrade last time,  I ran the script, - sh ./fglrx-uninstall.sh, then rebooted, ready to install the new GUI based driver that I had downloaded (atd i-driver-installer-9-5-x86.x86_64.run) But when it started up it froze because I had taken the driver away, I mean I could get into the safemode terminal screen. But not into the GUI wheere I would install the new driver.... so I don't make this mistake again wat do you ppl suggest I do and please break it down for this noob.

[COLOR=Orange](ATI MANUAL)
I have read teh ATI install manual

1 Launch the Terminal Application/Window and navigate to the /usr/share/ati folder.
  With superuser permissions, enter the command "sh ./fglrx-uninstall.sh".
2
  Reboot your system.
3[/COLOR]There is nothing sure in ATI case ... :) but I would logout from GUI, go to Terminal (Ctrl-LeftAlt-F1)and do it in this order (assuming that You have downloaded it in ~/Desktop) because I think that ATI driver installer can work also without GUI ... if it can not, no problem, since, at that time You have default driver working:
```
sudo sh ./fglrx-uninstall.sh
sudo dpkg-reconfigure -phigh xserver-xorg
sudo rm -r  /etc/ati/ (delete all possibly problematic setting You've accumulated in previuos use of ATI driver [http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6762440&postcount=1](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6762440&postcount=1))
cd ~/**D**esktop
sudo chmod +x ati-driver-installer-9-5-x86.x86_64.run
sudo sh ati-driver-installer-9-5-x86.x86_64.run
sudo aticonfig --initial -f
sudo reboot now
```Please do not hold me responsible for any possible problem, since I've not used ATI driver for some time ... open source got my love for the moment that lasts more than just a moment... :)

### Post by ssri on 2009-05-25
> **se_landy said:**
> I'm currently using driver from System->hardware drivers. It is ATI/AMD proprietary FGLRX driver, how can I know what version is that?? My graphics is not perfect, it's a bit slow, but it's usable... 
Can someone tell me where to find how to install that new ATI driver?? :) tnx :p

fire up the terminal:

~$more /var/log/Xorg.0.log | grep "Release Identifier"

mine is "(II) ATI Proprietary Linux Driver Release Identifier: 8.593"

meaning it is Catalyst 9.3

8.600 (and 8.602) = Catalyst 9.4

### Post by markbuntu on 2009-05-26
I have not used my Jaunty install a while but on my new Mandriva 2009.1 install I had a problem with slow rendering with fglrx which I fixed in xorg.conf with 

"Composite" "Enable"


My dual monitor xorg.conf is this

```

Section "ServerLayout"
	Identifier     "Default Layout"
	Screen      0  "aticonfig-Screen[0]-0" 0 0
EndSection

Section "Files"
EndSection

Section "Module"
EndSection

Section "ServerFlags"
	Option	    "Xinerama" "on"
EndSection


Section "Monitor"
	Identifier   "aticonfig-Monitor[0]-0"
	Option	    "VendorName" "ATI Proprietary Driver"
	Option	    "ModelName" "Generic Autodetecting Monitor"
	Option	    "DPMS" "true"
EndSection

Section "Monitor"
	Identifier   "aticonfig-Monitor[0]-1"
	Option	    "VendorName" "ATI Proprietary Driver"
	Option	    "ModelName" "Generic Autodetecting Monitor"
	Option	    "DPMS" "true"
EndSection

Section "Device"
	Identifier  "aticonfig-Device[0]-0"
	Driver      "fglrx"
	Option	    "EnableRandR12" "false"
	Option	    "DesktopSetup" "horizontal,reverse"
	BusID       "PCI:1:0:0"
EndSection

Section "Device"
	Identifier  "aticonfig-Device[0]-1"
	Driver      "fglrx"
	BusID       "PCI:1:0:0"
	Screen      1
EndSection

Section "Screen"
	Identifier "Default Screen"
	Device     "Configured Video Device"
	Monitor    "Configured Monitor"
EndSection

Section "Screen"
	Identifier "aticonfig-Screen[0]-0"
	Device     "aticonfig-Device[0]-0"
	Monitor    "aticonfig-Monitor[0]-0"
	DefaultDepth     24
	SubSection "Display"
		Viewport   0 0
		Depth     24
	EndSubSection
EndSection

Section "Screen"
	Identifier "aticonfig-Screen[0]-1"
	Device     "aticonfig-Device[0]-1"
	Monitor    "aticonfig-Monitor[0]-1"
	DefaultDepth     24
	SubSection "Display"
		Viewport   0 0
		Depth     24
	EndSubSection
EndSection

Section "Extensions"
	Option	    "Composite" "Enable"
EndSection

```

There are definitely some things wrong with that, but it works for me. I was getting messages in my Xorg.0.log that xrander would not allow the aticonfig --dtp=horizontal,reverse big desktop so I added the

Option	  "EnableRandR12" "false"

restarted x and then I could use aticonfig dtp=horizontal,reverse and it wrote the xorg.conf above leaving in the 

Option	  "EnableRandR12" "false"

I should probably try it with "Xinerama" "off" to see if that fixes the full screen across both monitors issue but it was the ONLY way I could get my two monitors into big desktop with KDE4. 

I am using a HD36501GB and 24 and 20 inch monitors.

### Post by HavocXphere on 2009-05-27

No, I don't think ATI is to blame in this case. I reckon its a xorg issue. Something with the new 1.6 Xorg is not agreeing with the standard way in which ati does its driver thing. (I'm guessing)

Some people are reporting that the problem can be fixed by patching Xorg.
[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/fglrx-installer/+bug/351186](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/fglrx-installer/+bug/351186)
(Warning: Some people are reporting that it trashed their box)

See also:
[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/fglrx-installer/+bug/351186/comments/80](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/fglrx-installer/+bug/351186/comments/80)

### Post by lswartz on 2009-05-27
> **zika said:**
> There is nothing sure in ATI case ... :) but I would logout from GUI, go to Terminal (Ctrl-LeftAlt-F1)and do it in this order (assuming that You have downloaded it in ~/Desktop) because I think that ATI driver installer can work also without GUI ... if it can not, no problem, since, at that time You have default driver working:
```
sudo sh ./fglrx-uninstall.sh
sudo dpkg-reconfigure -phigh xserver-xorg
sudo rm -r  /etc/ati/ (delete all possibly problematic setting You've accumulated in previuos use of ATI driver [http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6762440&postcount=1](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6762440&postcount=1))
cd ~/**D**esktop
sudo chmod +x ati-driver-installer-9-5-x86.x86_64.run
sudo sh ati-driver-installer-9-5-x86.x86_64.run
sudo aticonfig --initial -f
sudo reboot now
```Please do not hold me responsible for any possible problem, since I've not used ATI driver for some time ... open source got my love for the moment that lasts more than just a moment... :)

### Post by deriamis on 2009-05-27

Yeah, it's not that hard to do once you have an understanding of how the packaging system works. You can include the lines below in you sources.list for my PPA if you want:

```
deb http://ppa.launchpad.net/deriamis/ppa/ubuntu jaunty main
deb-src http://ppa.launchpad.net/deriamis/ppa/ubuntu jaunty main
```

And you can get my key with:

```
sudo apt-key adv --recv-keys --keyserver keyserver.ubuntu.com 18A5BE3D
```

Feel free to use it. I'd love the input. Mind, you're in for a trip if you do, though. On 2.6.30, at least, you need to recompile the kernel with MSI support and follow a series of steps to get the install right:

[http://wiki.cchtml.com/index.php/Ubuntu_Jaunty_Installation_Guide](http://wiki.cchtml.com/index.php/Ubuntu_Jaunty_Installation_Guide)

Enjoy!

### Post by deriamis on 2009-05-29
> **markbuntu said:**
> Well the rt kernel will not boot for me in Jaunty or Intrepid so I cannot try it there. You wouldn't happen to have a build for Hardy amd64 lying around would you?

An RT kernel or fglrx-installer? In both cases, no, sorry. I could probably try to backport them, but that's easier said than done. The kernel would likely be incompatible with some of Hardy's drivers (ABI changes), so you would probably have issues there. I am currently making a build of Karmic's kernels right now if you want to wait for a while, though. It might be the case that Karmic's RT kernel doesn't cause problems for you - what are those problems, by the way?

As for fglrx, that's probably a no-go no matter what you do. It's only compatible with Jaunty's xorg server, and backporting xorg is something I don't know I have the stomach to do. The last time I dealt with fixing xorg, I spent three weeks at it and came out with nothing to show for it. That was back in the days when I thought Gentoo was the best distro, by the way. There's a reason I use Ubuntu now. You can try, though it might be better to try getting RT to boot first. That might be your paradoxical best-bet.

EDIT: I forgot to mention that the new fglrx is only going to be compatible with later kernels anyway - I think from 2.6.28 on. So you would have to somehow get a later kernel working in Hardy if that is what you are going to do. Maybe your issues can be resolved with it?

---

### Post by 10011010 on 2009-05-30
> **se_landy said:**
> I'm currently using driver from System->hardware drivers. It is ATI/AMD proprietary FGLRX driver, how can I know what version is that?? My graphics is not perfect, it's a bit slow, but it's usable... 
Can someone tell me where to find how to install that new ATI driver?? :) tnx :p

Just go to ati.amd.com, downloads/support, and download drivers.  Choose the x86 or x86_64 linux drivers and save that .run file.

Then in a shell, go ot the directory of that file and type:
```
 chmod 755 ati <press TAB> 
```

Then run to find what packages to build, in case it bombs the system:
```
 ./ati...run --listpkg 
```

It should be either Ubuntu/jaunty or Ubuntu/9.04, then use the --buildpkg parameter:
```
 ./ati...run --buildpkg Ubuntu/<jaunty or 9.04> 
```

This will build all .deb files that you can ```
dpkg -i *.deb
``` to install.  If it fails afterwards, you can uninstall the package created.

---

### Post by Minsky on 2009-05-30
Has anyone succeeded in getting a HD4830 running with the 9.5 drivers (or any other proprietary drivers for that matter) in Jaunty. If so, can you please explain how you did it otherwise my barber is going to wonder what's happened to me

---

### Post by deriamis on 2009-05-30
> **Minsky said:**
> Has anyone succeeded in getting a HD4830 running with the 9.5 drivers (or any other proprietary drivers for that matter) in Jaunty. If so, can you please explain how you did it otherwise my barber is going to wonder what's happened to me

Well, I can't speak to that card, but first try typing
```
sudo modprobe -r fglrx
sudo modprobe fglrx
```

And note whether it installs the module or not. If it doesn't, look at the last few lines of dmesg to see why.

If it did, then take a look at /var/log/Xorg.0.log and see why the server doesn't start. It might be something you can fix.

---

### Post by deriamis on 2009-05-31
Well, it turns out that I can't use the new Catalyst drivers anyway. Despite the fact that my card (Mobility Radeon 1250) is still listed in their compatibility list for 9.5, the driver gives me that error that it can't initialize the DRM. Which means compatibility for my card was actually taken out.

Well, crap. I don't like the open source driver because my screen flickers every time there is heavy disk activity, and the *other* open source driver (radeonhd) won't detect the LCD on my laptop properly.

I just have one thing to say about all this: ATI on Linux is a dead concept. I love AMD, and I think ATI's cards are better than NVIDIA's, but compatibility is king. AMD really needs to stop ATI's burning desire for binary-only drivers. And the open-source drivers aren't much better, but that's not their fault - it still doesn't help me, though.

Well, I managed to get a module insertion problem out of the way before I came up with the short end of the stick here. You won't get any "missing symbol" errors on insertion anymore (I hope). So feel free to use the latest-and-greatest drivers I have just put into my PPA if you want, and let me know if there are any problems with it. I'll still keep it updated as long as I can. And ask me questions if you have problems, too - I (unfortunately) have lots of experience with ATI in Linux.

### Post by Minsky on 2009-05-31
Also, this is the contents of xorg.conf:

```

# xorg.conf (X.Org X Window System server configuration file)
#
# This file was generated by dexconf, the Debian X Configuration tool, using
# values from the debconf database.
#
# Edit this file with caution, and see the xorg.conf manual page.
# (Type "man xorg.conf" at the shell prompt.)
#
# This file is automatically updated on xserver-xorg package upgrades *only*
# if it has not been modified since the last upgrade of the xserver-xorg
# package.
#
# Note that some configuration settings that could be done previously
# in this file, now are automatically configured by the server and settings
# here are ignored.
#
# If you have edited this file but would like it to be automatically updated
# again, run the following command:
#   sudo dpkg-reconfigure -phigh xserver-xorg

Section "ServerLayout"
	Identifier     "aticonfig Layout"
	Screen      0  "aticonfig-Screen[0]-0" 0 0
EndSection

Section "Files"
EndSection

Section "Module"
EndSection

Section "Monitor"
	Identifier   "aticonfig-Monitor[0]-0"
	Option	    "VendorName" "ATI Proprietary Driver"
	Option	    "ModelName" "Generic Autodetecting Monitor"
	Option	    "DPMS" "true"
EndSection

Section "Device"
	Identifier  "aticonfig-Device[0]-0"
	Driver      "fglrx"
	Option	    "UseFastTLS" "1"
	BusID       "PCI:1:0:0"
EndSection

Section "Screen"
	Identifier "aticonfig-Screen[0]-0"
	Device     "aticonfig-Device[0]-0"
	Monitor    "aticonfig-Monitor[0]-0"
	DefaultDepth     24
	SubSection "Display"
		Viewport   0 0
		Depth     24
	EndSubSection
EndSection

```

Any help would be really, really appreciated.

[  847.100158] fglrx: module license 'Proprietary. (C) 2002 - ATI Technologies, Starnberg, GERMANY' taints kernel.
[  847.145198] [fglrx] Maximum main memory to use for locked dma buffers: 3126 MBytes.
[  847.145508] [fglrx]   vendor: 1002 device: 944c count: 1
[  847.146065] [fglrx] ioport: bar 4, base 0xb000, size: 0x100
[  847.146074] pci 0000:01:00.0: setting latency timer to 64
[  847.148257] [fglrx] Driver built-in PAT support is enabled successfully
[  847.148268] [fglrx:firegl_init_module] *ERROR* firegl_stub_register failed
```

Not that I think it's actually the cause of your problems, but did you also install the fglrx-modaliases package? That can cause problems if it's not installed. Also, you might want to check the compatibility for your card. Usually, when the driver can't initialize the gpu, that means compatibility has been taken out of the driver. I sure hope that's not the case, though.

### Post by sciurognathi on 2009-05-31
Minsky you are close and as I already succeeded I recommend my way.
First edit xorg.conf and delete all lines and get rid of fglrx: ```
sudo apt-get remove --purge xorg-driver-fglrx
```If you receive messages do what it is neccessary.
Now, install the newest linux-headers-2.6.28-12-generic and rest (for x64 do not forget ia32-libs). Restart with the new kernel and do: ```
sh ati...run --extract ati
cd ati
sudo sh packages/Ubuntu/ati-packager.sh --buildpkg jaunty
sudo sh packages/Ubuntu/ati-packager.sh --installpkg jaunty
```Note the messages after buildpkg and do what it is neccessary (you will need to copy the fglrx-rt-compat.patch from ../patches/patches to ../patches). Make another buildpkg. Than do ```
sudo aticonfig --initial
```and you are ready to go.
If you have questions I will answer in the next 24h.

---

### Post by deriamis on 2009-06-01
> **Ethelbert2 said:**
> [COLOR="DarkGreen"][FONT="Tahoma"]I am still a relative beginner (tried Linux two years ago - just returned) and confused by the technical detail above, though it is a useful thread. 2 Some of the posts relate to uninstalling stuff like fglrx- will I need to do that and before or after using the ATI run file.?

Many thanks and hoping the questions make sense



[/FONT][/COLOR]__

Ah! Welcome!

1) No, that's a lot of technical detail for people who have problems. From what I remember, your card should be well-supported by the new ATI drivers if it's a newer card. If it's older, say about 3 years old or in a laptop older than two years, you might have problems with the new driver. If you use Ubuntu packages, you won't have to worry all that much about dependencies.

2) Yes, you do need to do those uninstalls. We have something just a couple of posts ago that tells you how. Make sure you remove the old radeon and radeonhd drivers before you get started as well, or you can just about guarantee problems!

Try the packages I posted earlier. They, along with those directions, should help you out. About the last thing you want to be doing as a beginner is compiling packages - let that wait until you have a bit more familiarity with the system. Don't let me stop you if you think you're ready, though. The only way to learn Linux is by doing.

The Jaunty version of Catalyst is actually a bit behind where ATI is. I'm guessing that you have a newer card that wasn't officially supported by Catalyst by the time MOTU put it into the tree, so that may be your problem. One thing no Linux doesn't have problems with is ATI video cards.

As for the multiple resolutions issue - well, that's something you're going to have to speak with amdcccle on (make sure you start it with gksudo!). Don't try using mere XrandR with an ATI card, or you will be very sorry. Catalyst likes doing that kind of thing by itself.

### Post by deriamis on 2009-06-04
> **pandasonic said:**
> I just wanted to post my xorg.conf file here, I was at work when I first posted.

```
Section "ServerLayout"
	Identifier     "aticonfig Layout"
	Screen      0  "aticonfig-Screen[0]-0" 0 0
EndSection

Section "Files"
EndSection

Section "Module"
	Load  "glx"
EndSection

Section "Monitor"
	Identifier   "aticonfig-Monitor[0]-0"
	Option	    "VendorName" "ATI Proprietary Driver"
	Option	    "ModelName" "Generic Autodetecting Monitor"
	Option	    "DPMS" "true"
EndSection

Section "Device"
	Identifier  "aticonfig-Device[0]-0"
	Driver      "fglrx"
	BusID       "PCI:1:0:0"
EndSection

Section "Screen"
	Identifier "aticonfig-Screen[0]-0"
	Device     "aticonfig-Device[0]-0"
	Monitor    "aticonfig-Monitor[0]-0"
	DefaultDepth     24
	SubSection "Display"
		Viewport   0 0
		Depth     24
	EndSubSection
EndSection

```

Basically, I cannot log out of my system (ever).  Also, hibernate/suspend and sometimes even restarting do not work if Compiz is enabled.

What do I seem to be doing wrong?

Nothing at all. It's probably just something you aren't doing at all. Welcome to the fun that is ATI on Linux.

Seriously, though, you should probably be using Catalyst 9.5 if your card is new. The first thing you try when using proprietary drivers is to use the most up-to-date driver your card will support. This is something ATI will tell you every time. There are any number of reasons why you could be having these problems, but a driver that wasn't written specifically to deal with your card is one of them. (If your card is two or more years old, disregard this advice.)

Next, you should be using amdcccle to configure your screen area, and NOT the Ubuntu-supplied stuff. It's a pain, but that's ATI. fglrx doesn't play by the rules at all; it only gives XRandR the barest of nods and all that OpenGL stuff is on its terms and not how X wants it.

Third, and probably important in this case, Xorg is having some uncharacteristic stability problems of late. Especially in the case of the Catalyst drivers, you can find all sorts of problems with GL rendering. Part of that is because the fglrx driver tries to use on-the-edge code to get its job done and X doesn't always like it. Make sure you are using either EXA or UXA acceleration in your xorg.conf with newer Catalyst drivers (EXA is more stable with Catalyst right now).

Lastly, make sure you know which options you should and should not use in your xorg.conf file before editing it. Again, welcome to the fun that is ATI on Linux - you'll never know unless someone before you has walked the path. I haven't used a newer ATI card on X in quite some time, but in general, if you have an IGP, you should be defining the amount of memory the card will use, even if you have it defined in the BIOS. fglrx doesn't always get it right, especially if you have a buggy BIOS. Some other things you might set are overlay options (yes, even if fglrx is supposed to pick the "right" one) and the like. Sometimes, fglrx works just fine right out of the box, and sometimes other people need to tweak it a lot. Again, welcome to the fun that is ATI on Linux.

Now, you might also try the radeon and radeonhd drivers as well. They aren't as glitzy as the Catalyst drivers, but they do tend to be a bit better understood by the Open Source community, and problems are therefore more easily fixed. If you have an older card, you don't have an option at all, really. You have to use the Open Source drivers in that case.

As to your specific problems, pandasonic, I can tell you that your xorg.conf file is correct by all appearances. You might just have to make it more correct. Try updating to the newest Catalyst if you can, and then try to add options one-by-one until you get it right. Start with the memory options if you have an IGP and then add an overlay option or two. Make sure you have the driver using EXA as well. Above that, we'd have to find a guru on your specific card (and now I wish I hadn't lost that website!).

---

### Post by Melcar on 2009-06-04
The ATI proprietary drivers (fglrx) can only use XAA.  And xrandr does work with fglrx.

@pandasonic:

You got an HD4770, which is not supported by the drivers in Jaunty (reason for the watermark), and the famous "same day support" with the latest driver, meaning that while the card is recognized, it won't really function right and you may experience some issues.  The next driver release, 9.6, should have proper support for the card.  
Once you install the driver and initialize the module (*aticonfig --initial*), fglrx configures everything it needs to on xorg.conf; you usually don't have to do any extra changes to the file, specially not on these newer cards.  The driver will load its default settings, which are what usually work for most.
For further configuration, it's best to use CCCLE (gosh, I wish they would do a GTK version of it, or at least port it over to qt4), since most configuration options are already laid out there.  If that doesn't work, you can try command line based configuration; if you type *aticonfig* in a terminal, you will be given several configuration options for the driver that you can use.
None of the open source drivers supports your card yet (not even the latest builds), so for you they are not an option (right now).  Primary support should be added soon thought.  Functioning 3D for the HD series of cards is still a ways off, but hopefully by years end we have something that we can use.

---

### Post by Melcar on 2009-06-04
I don't know why people keep insisting on hacking the driver and all its files.  They usually end up worse than before.

After you install the driver (using ATI's script) *all* you need to do to initialize it is *sudo aticonfig --initial*.  This generates a new xorg.conf with the necessary options, and the original is backed up.  After this all you need to do is reboot (or restart X, but rebooting works better).  You don't need to bother with amdpcsb at all; all changes are done either in CCCLE or with aticonfig, which write all the changes to amdpcsdb.  Changing settings directly in amdpcsdb almost always leads to problems because the damn file is not documented; no one aside from ATI devs. know how to manually configure it, and the people that claim to know are guessing or got results by trial and error.
If you for some reason messed up the file and/or want to completely remove the driver and start fresh, this is what you do:

- Run the uninstall script
- Remove /etc/ati (this is where amdpcsdb is)
- Generate a new xorg.conf file (or restore the backed up one) and make sure you load the open source driver (a lot of people forget to do this and end up with a black screen at log-in)
- Reboot

Next time you log-in, all traces of fglrx will be gone, and you will have a fresh xorg.conf.  Now you can re-install the driver and not worry about persistent configuration files.

---

- Generate a new xorg.conf file (or restore the backed up one) and make sure you load the open source driver (a lot of people forget to do this and end up with a black screen at log-in)+1 (for the whole post) (I say that after hours wasted on trial and error so this is kind of "self-critic" ... :) )

### Post by deriamis on 2009-06-04
> **Melcar said:**
> I don't know why people keep insisting on hacking the driver and all its files.  They usually end up worse than before.

We do it because we've had to. For most people not using HD cards, the defaults work beautifully. The problem is, ATI never bothered to properly support HD cards in Linux. So we have to mess with things a bit. Not all the options available to the fglrx driver are configurable through either aticonfig or cccle, so we have to resort to desperate measures. I'm all for using the radeonhd driver, but that is lacking for some cards as well. We're in a bind.

> **Melcar said:**
> After you install the driver (using ATI's script) *all* you need to do to initialize it is *sudo aticonfig --initial*.  This generates a new xorg.conf with the necessary options, and the original is backed up.  After this all you need to do is reboot (or restart X, but rebooting works better).  You don't need to bother with amdpcsb at all; all changes are done either in CCCLE or with aticonfig, which write all the changes to amdpcsdb.  Changing settings directly in amdpcsdb almost always leads to problems because the damn file is not documented; no one aside from ATI devs. know how to manually configure it, and the people that claim to know are guessing or got results by trial and error.

Yes, we are guessing, and the results are by trial and error. That's rather the point. The Catalyst drivers are a nightmare, and ATI's insistence on not playing by the rules is making the situation worse. For those unlucky bastards (like me) who have a card not 100% supported by ATI and the Catalyst drivers, futzing around with things is what we're left with. It's not so much a question of user stupidity but of proper support when people have to do unsupported things. And the constant canard we get from developers and manufacturers that "we develop primarily for Windows but we do provide Linux support" is utter crap. It shouldn't matter what's most popular with your users - if you are developing hardware that runs on computers that can also run Linux, you have to accept the fact some of your users will run Linux.

Hence, the recent support by AMD of the radeonhd drivers. Problem is, the radeonhd drivers just aren't there yet. So those of us who never have had proper support are left trying to make things work by guessing and trial-and-error.

> **Melcar said:**
> If you for some reason messed up the file and/or want to completely remove the driver and start fresh, this is what you do:

- Run the uninstall script
- Remove /etc/ati (this is where amdpcsdb is)
- Generate a new xorg.conf file (or restore the backed up one) and make sure you load the open source driver (a lot of people forget to do this and end up with a black screen at log-in)
- Reboot

Next time you log-in, all traces of fglrx will be gone, and you will have a fresh xorg.conf.  Now you can re-install the driver and not worry about persistent configuration files.

Better idea: do all the above and see if radeonhd works for you. There's a post about doing so:

[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/RadeonHD]("https://help.ubuntu.com/community/RadeonHD")

But I can't help but think this is all just so much more guessing.

### Post by Melcar on 2009-06-04
The HD cards are among the best supported and this will only get better.  That's the main reason older cards were dropped.  The chips where the driver had problems were on the older, pre 1Kxxx ones, because it would load defaults that worked for the HD series.
There is no reason to mess around with amdpcsdb because everything is configurable with either CCCLE or aticonfig.  Those two are the configuration tools that write everything back to amdpcsdb and xorg.conf, and they are documented.  Hacking amdpsdb (if you do it right) yields the same results as those two; the problem is that most don't know how to and end up messing up their driver.
And if anything, it's the green team that does not play by the rules.  Both Intel and AMD/ATI actually care and make efforts to support Linux proper.

### Post by deriamis on 2009-06-04

Those two are the configuration tools that write everything back to amdpcsdb and xorg.conf, and they are documented.  Hacking amdpsdb (if you do it right) yields the same results as those two; the problem is that most don't know how to and end up messing up their driver.

My experience hasn't been yours with HD cards. Then, it's been a while since I tried. See, I got a bit pissed off when the new ATI card I bought refused to work in Linux, even with Catalyst drivers. Besides which, I think you have it a bit backwards here: AMD does and always did support Linux. ATI very much did not, and AMD is trying to fix that. Linux users have been complaining for years that the binary drivers that ATI released were below par.

And no, there is no way you can claim that fglrx plays by the rules when most of the configuration is manipulated using custom tools outside the purview of the X server, when those same configuration settings could just as well be set in the xorg.conf file itself. That's why the new radeonhd driver is being developed with support from AMD, you know - yes, it's true that the HD cards have the best Linux support, but that doesn't count for much at the moment when that support is still under development. It's great that it's finally happening, but the people who need their cards supported are left in the lurch.

As for configuring fglrx, yes, you are right to raise your objections. The problem is, Catalyst does not support HD cards very well at all. If it did, we would have 3D support on them. The problem here is that, at least on Linux, the newer cards have very buggy support at best. We have to wait for a couple of iterations of binary releases before anything is stable. For quite a time, that meant a long wait. Only now with the radeonhd driver is that changing, but again, that doesn't count for much when the driver is still under heavy debelopment.

### Post by Melcar on 2009-06-04
Fglrx plays by the rules as much as a proprietary blob can.  Can't say the same for nvidia's blob, which replaces most of X (and that is the smallest of offenses it's guilty off).  Not everything is documented, but that's expected from a proprietary driver.  It relies on its own tools for configuration, but you can still use X configuration tools with acceptable results.
Fglrx does provide good 2D/3D support for all cards it supports.  3D performance in Linux is on par with Windows performance, and the driver has accepable 2D acceleration despite it using older tools.  Yes, it currently has troubles with composite managers, but so do most drivers at the moment.

---

### Post by markbuntu on 2009-06-04
AMD bought ATI not very long ago and has been pushing them to make linux support as good as windows ever since, These things take time. You can cry about the loss of support for older cards but that is very temporary as the open drivers have full 2D and 3D for all those cards and they are rapidly improving. 

Just because a distribution has crappy support for your older card does not mean the driver has not been improved since distributions do not generally update the drivers from code freeze which can be months before the distribution is released.

Don't feel so bad. ATI also dropped those cards from future windows drivers as well and there is no open drivers for windows users to fall back on.

### Post by Minsky on 2009-06-05
> **sciurognathi said:**
> Minsky you are close and as I already succeeded I recommend my way.
First edit xorg.conf and delete all lines and get rid of fglrx: ```
sudo apt-get remove --purge xorg-driver-fglrx
```If you receive messages do what it is neccessary.
Now, install the newest linux-headers-2.6.28-12-generic and rest (for x64 do not forget ia32-libs). Restart with the new kernel and do: ```
sh ati...run --extract ati
cd ati
sudo sh packages/Ubuntu/ati-packager.sh --buildpkg jaunty
sudo sh packages/Ubuntu/ati-packager.sh --installpkg jaunty
```Note the messages after buildpkg and do what it is neccessary (you will need to copy the fglrx-rt-compat.patch from ../patches/patches to ../patches). Make another buildpkg. Than do ```
sudo aticonfig --initial
```and you are ready to go.
If you have questions I will answer in the next 24h.
